## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables (stress sigma, strain epsilon, temperature T) indicate a constitutive law for a solid where mechanical response depends on deformation and thermal state. Typical relationships include linear/thermoelasticity, nonlinear hardening (plasticity), and temperature-dependent softening of modulus or flow stress.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elastic (Hooke’s law): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus decreases with temperature)
- Thermoelastic strain shift (thermal expansion): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T - c2) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal strain/reference offset)
- Nonlinear elastic (quadratic/cubic elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate strain nonlinearity)
- Hyperelastic exponential form: sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (rubber-like/finite-strain stiffening)
- Logarithmic stiffening: sigma = c0 * log(c1 * epsilon + 1) (incremental stiffening with diminishing slope at larger strain)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type implicit/explicit stress form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (smooth transition from linear to nonlinear hardening)
- Ludwik/Hollomon hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (strain hardening multiplied by temperature softening)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening saturates at large strain)
- Voce hardening with temperature softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon))) * exp(-c3 * T) (saturating hardening and thermal softening combined)
- Johnson–Cook-like separable form (without normalization): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (empirical plastic flow stress with thermal softening factor)
- Eyring/thermal-activation-like stress dependence: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(-c2 * T) (smooth nonlinear response with thermal activation/softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma proportional to epsilon suggests sigma ≈ E(T) * epsilon, with E(T) slowly varying in T.
- Thermal softening: factors like exp(-c * T) or (1 - c * T**m) multiplying a strain-dependent term represent decreasing strength/stiffness with rising temperature.
- Thermal expansion offset: structures sigma = E * (epsilon - c * T - c) indicate an apparent shift of the zero-stress strain with temperature.
- Strain hardening signature: sigma increasing faster than linear in epsilon (e.g., epsilon**n with n > 1) indicates work hardening/plastic contribution.
- Hardening saturation: terms (1 - exp(-c * epsilon)) indicate rapid initial hardening that levels off at large strain.
- Finite-strain stiffening: exp(c * epsilon) growth suggests strong stiffening typical of hyperelastic/chain stretching behavior.
- Diminishing incremental stiffness: log(1 + c * epsilon) indicates increasing stress but decreasing tangent modulus with strain.
- Separable thermomechanical response: sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) often implies temperature changes scale the overall stress level without strongly changing the strain-shape.

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c3*exp(-c4/(c5*T)) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is a sum of three terms with a very specific structure in **two variables** (epsilon, T):

1) \(2.0970\;\epsilon^3\)

2) \(71.3556\;\epsilon^{0.1998}\exp\!\left(-\dfrac{5.0029}{8.314\,T}\right)\)  (note: exponential depends on \(1/T\), not on \(\epsilon\))

3) \(3.3046\;\epsilon^3\,(T-370.1712)=3.3046\,T\,\epsilon^3 - (3.3046\cdot 370.1712)\epsilon^3\)

So overall GT is **affine in \(T\)** with coefficients that are functions of \(\epsilon\), and it contains a distinctive \(\exp(-\text{const}/T)\) factor multiplied by \(\epsilon^{0.1998}\).

A candidate can only match if it can reproduce:
- a \(T\epsilon^3\) term and an \(\epsilon^3\) term (polynomial in \(\epsilon\)),
- plus a term \(\epsilon^{a}\exp(-b/T)\) with \(a\approx 0.1998\),
under some plausible domain restriction (e.g., \(T>0\), \(\epsilon>0\)).

### Candidate 1
\(T c0 \epsilon^{c1} + c2\epsilon^2 + \frac{c3\epsilon}{c4\epsilon+c5} + \frac{c6}{c5+\epsilon} + c7\epsilon + c8 + c9\epsilon^{c1}\)

- Has a \(T\epsilon^{c1}\) term and an \(\epsilon^{c1}\) term: could set \(c1=3\) to mimic the \(T\epsilon^3\) and \(\epsilon^3\) pieces.

**No match.**

### Summary of why none can match
To match GT, a candidate must (at minimum) be able to express:
- a term proportional to \(T\epsilon^3\),
- a term proportional to \(\epsilon^3\),
- and a term proportional to \(\epsilon^{0.1998}\exp(-\text{const}/T)\).

No candidate contains the required \(\exp(-\text{const}/T)\) structure. The only \(T\)-exponentials present are \(\exp(\text{const}\cdot T)\), which cannot be made identical to \(\exp(-b/T)\) on any nontrivial continuous domain by choosing constants. Also, most candidates do not depend on \(T\) at all.

I need to analyze whether any candidate can match the Ground Truth (GT):

$$GT = 2.097\epsilon^3 + 71.356\epsilon^{0.2}\exp\left(\frac{-5.003}{8.314T}\right) + 3.305\epsilon^3(T - 370.17)$$

Key observations about GT:
- It has an $\epsilon^3$ term (polynomial in epsilon)
- It has an $\epsilon^{0.2}$ term (fractional power of epsilon) multiplied by $\exp(-\text{const}/T)$
- It has a $T\epsilon^3$ term (interaction between T and epsilon)
- The T dependence appears in two ways: through $\exp(-c/T)$ and linearly as $T\epsilon^3$

Let me simplify: GT = $(2.097 - 3.305 \times 370.17)\epsilon^3 + 3.305T\epsilon^3 + 71.356\epsilon^{0.2}\exp(-0.6018/T)$

This means GT has:
1. A term proportional to $T\epsilon^3$
2. A term proportional to $\epsilon^3$
3. A term proportional to $\epsilon^{0.2}\exp(-\text{const}/T)$

Now I need to check each candidate for the presence of T dependence and the correct functional forms.

**Critical filter: T dependence.** Most candidates have NO T variable at all. The GT requires T dependence (both $T\epsilon^3$ and $\exp(-c/T)$). Let me scan for candidates with T:

- **Candidate 1**: Has $T*c0*\epsilon^{c1}$ — linear T dependence ✓, but no $\exp(-c/T)$ term. Cannot match the $\exp(-c/T)$ term. **NO MATCH**
- **Candidate 6**: Has $\exp(T*c9)$ — this is $\exp(cT)$, not $\exp(-c/T)$. **NO MATCH**
- **Candidate 7**: Has $T*c0$ — linear T but no epsilon coupling, no $\exp(-c/T)$. **NO MATCH**
- **Candidate 36**: Has $T*c0/(c1\epsilon+c2)$ — T dependence but wrong form. No $\exp(-c/T)$. **NO MATCH**
- **Candidate 39**: Has $\exp(T*c6)$ — wrong form of T dependence. **NO MATCH**

All other candidates (2-5, 8-35, 37-50) have NO T variable at all. Since GT fundamentally depends on T in two distinct ways ($T\epsilon^3$ and $\exp(-c/T)$), and these cannot be eliminated (the coefficients are non-zero), none of these candidates can match.

Let me verify candidates 1, 6, 7, 36, 39 more carefully:

**Candidate 1**: $T c_0\epsilon^{c_1} + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_3\epsilon/(c_4\epsilon+c_5) + c_6/(c_5+\epsilon) + c_7\epsilon + c_8 + c_9\epsilon^{c_1}$
- Has $T\epsilon^{c_1}$ but no $\exp(-c/T)$. The $\epsilon^{0.2}\exp(-0.6/T)$ term cannot be represented. **NO MATCH**
